<div class=Section5>

<h1><a name="_Toc7851583"></a><a name="_Toc7919079"></a><a name="_Toc7919446"></a><a
name="_Toc7924635"></a><a name="_Toc7972121"><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7924635'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919446'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919079'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7851583'><![if !supportLists]>1.0<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Introduction</span></span></span></span></a></h1>

<p class=MsoNormal><a name="_Toc476378719"></a><a name="_Toc7506162"></a><a
name="_Toc7511952"><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7506162'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc476378719'><span style='font-size:11.0pt'>The report
was prepared by the Constellation-X project in response to a request for
information from the SEU Roadmap Technology Subcommittee appointed by the
National Aeronautics and Space Administration Headquarters</span>.</span></span></a></p>

<h2><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511952'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7506162'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc476378719'><a name="_Toc7514605"></a><a
name="_Toc7593036"></a><a name="_Toc7593124"></a><a name="_Toc7837407"></a><a
name="_Toc7846478"></a><a name="_Toc7851584"></a><a name="_Toc7919080"></a><a
name="_Toc7919447"></a><a name="_Toc7924636"></a><a name="_Toc7972122"><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7924636'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919447'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919080'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7851584'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7846478'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7837407'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593124'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593036'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514605'><![if !supportLists]>1.1.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Purpose</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></span></span></span></h2>

<p class=MsoNormal><a name="_Toc461942474"></a><a name="_Toc462013685"></a><a
name="_Toc462014471"></a><a name="_Toc462015013"></a><a name="_Toc462017103"><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc462015013'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc462014471'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc462013685'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc461942474'><span
style='font-size:11.0pt'>The purpose o</span></span></span></span></span></a><a
name="_Toc476378720"></a><a name="_Toc7506163"></a><a name="_Toc7511953"><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7506163'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc476378720'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc461942474'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc462013685'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc462014471'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc462015013'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc462017103'><span style='font-size:11.0pt'>f this
document is to provide a response to the seven questions submitted by the SEU
Roadmap Technology Subcommittee:<o:p></o:p></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></p>

<ol style='margin-top:0in' start=1 type=1>
 <li class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:4.0pt;margin-bottom:8.0pt;mso-list:l8 level1 lfo71;
     tab-stops:list .5in'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511953'><span
     style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7506163'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc476378720'><span

     style='mso-bookmark:_Toc462017103'><b>What are the Level 1 and Level 2
     science requirements for the proposed mission, and how do these motivate
     the candidate technologies which will be investigated?<span
     style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Explain the connections between
     the science requirements and the engineering requirements on those
     technologies.<o:p></o:p></b></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li>
 <li class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:4.0pt;margin-bottom:8.0pt;mso-list:l8 level1 lfo71;
     tab-stops:list .5in'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511953'><span
     style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7506163'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc476378720'><span
     style='mso-bookmark:_Toc461942474'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc462013685'><span
     style='mso-bookmark:_Toc462014471'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc462015013'><span
     style='mso-bookmark:_Toc462017103'><b>What are the significant
     technological challenges for these technologies --- i.e., which technical
     capabilities have not already been demonstrated?<o:p></o:p></b></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li>
</ol>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='margin-top:4.0pt;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:
8.0pt;margin-left:.5in;text-indent:-.25in;mso-list:l8 level1 lfo71'><span

</span></span><![endif]><span style='font-style:normal'>For each technological
challenge, what are the metrics by which success --- i.e., technical readiness
--- is to be measured?<o:p></o:p></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p>

<ol style='margin-top:0in' start=4 type=1>
 <li class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:4.0pt;margin-bottom:8.0pt;mso-list:l8 level1 lfo71;
     tab-stops:list .5in'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511953'><span

     required to validate technical readiness? Will ground testing be
     sufficient, or are there technical capabilities which can only be
     demonstrated in space?<o:p></o:p></b></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li>
</ol>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='margin-top:4.0pt;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:

</span></span><![endif]><span style='font-style:normal'>What is status of each
metric --- i.e., compare the current capability with the required capability?<o:p></o:p></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p>

 <li class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:4.0pt;margin-bottom:8.0pt;mso-list:l8 level1 lfo71;

     significant advancement or new approach?<o:p></o:p></b></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li>

<h2><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511953'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7506163'><span

</span><![endif]>Document Organization</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></h2>

<span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc462017103'></span><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc462015013'></span><span

to the SEU Subcommittees questions are organized into nine sections (Sections

<h1><a name="_Toc7851586"></a><a name="_Toc7919082"></a><a name="_Toc7919449"></a><a
name="_Toc7924638"></a><a name="_Toc7972124"><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7924638'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919449'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919082'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7851586'><![if !supportLists]>2.0<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Response to Questions</span></span></span></span></a></h1>

<h2><a name="_Toc7851587"></a><a name="_Toc7919083"></a><a name="_Toc7919450"></a><a
name="_Toc7924639"></a><a name="_Toc7972125"><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7924639'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919450'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919083'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7851587'><![if !supportLists]>2.1.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Top-Level Response to Question 1</span></span></span></span></a></h2>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>1.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What are the Level 1 and Level 2 science requirements for the
proposed mission, and how do these motivate the candidate technologies which
will be investigated?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Explain the
connections between the science requirements and the engineering requirements
on those technologies.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The key Science Objectives for the Constellation-X Mission
are:</p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:8.0pt;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:4.0pt;
margin-left:1.0in;text-indent:-.5in;mso-list:l22 level1 lfo58;tab-stops:list 1.0in'><![if !supportLists]><span
style='font-size:11.0pt'><b>I.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></b></span><![endif]><span style='font-size:11.0pt'><b>Measure the X-ray
spectra of the faintest sources in the Roentgen Satellite (ROSAT) Deep Surveys
and the Chandra deep fields in less than 10<sup>5 </sup>seconds. <o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:8.0pt;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:4.0pt;
margin-left:1.0in;text-indent:-.5in;mso-list:l22 level1 lfo58;tab-stops:list 1.0in'><![if !supportLists]><span
style='font-size:11.0pt'><b>II.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></b></span><![endif]><span style='font-size:11.0pt'><b>Test General
Relativity in the strong gravity limit by mapping the inner emission regions of
black holes.<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:8.0pt;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:4.0pt;
margin-left:1.0in;text-indent:-.5in;mso-list:l22 level1 lfo58;tab-stops:list 1.0in'><![if !supportLists]><span
style='font-size:11.0pt'><b>III.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></b></span><![endif]><span style='font-size:11.0pt'><b>Search for the
dark matter or missing baryons from observations of the Intergalactic
Medium (IGM)<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class=MsoNormal style='margin-top:8.0pt;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:4.0pt;
margin-left:1.0in;text-indent:-.5in;mso-list:l22 level1 lfo58;tab-stops:list 1.0in'><![if !supportLists]><span
style='font-size:11.0pt'><b>IV.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></b></span><![endif]><span style='font-size:11.0pt'><b>Study the
interchange of matter and energy between stars and the Interstellar Medium
(ISM), and the enrichment of the IGM and Intracluster Medium (ICM) and the
evolution of clusters of galaxies.<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>As part of the mission definition effort, a series of
specific science goals were developed to help define the specific mission
requirements. <span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;</span>A few examples of
these observations are:</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l40 level1 lfo80;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Determine the rotation rate and mass of the black holes
using Doppler shifts, relativistic broadening, and reverberation analysis of
iron K lines from the innermost regions of the accretion disks.</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l40 level1 lfo80;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Determine the geometry of the accretion flow in Active
Galactic Nuclei (AGN) by observing Compton reflection, partial covering, and
absorption by inflowing and outflowing material.</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l40 level1 lfo80;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Measure the gravitational redshift at the surface of
white dwarfs in magnetic cataclysmic variables (CVs) using the iron K
fluorescence lines.</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l40 level1 lfo80;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Investigate the evolution of clusters by determining
the abundance, density, and temperature structure for a large sample of
clusters at low and high redshifts (z &gt; 0.5). </p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l40 level1 lfo80;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Directly map the velocity profile of cooling flows and
determine their relationship to the dominant central galaxy. </p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l40 level1 lfo80;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Constrain cosmological parameters by measuring X-ray
line absorption through hot gas in clusters of galaxies using background active
galactic nuclei.</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l40 level1 lfo80;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Set limits on the cosmological density of a hot diffuse
intergalactic medium via an X-ray Gunn-Peterson test using edge and line
opacity in the soft X-ray band. </p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l40 level1 lfo80;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Investigate the evolution of the intergalactic medium
by determining the chemical abundances at a large window of redshifts.</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l40 level1 lfo80;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Use non-thermal signatures to identify sites of cosmic
ray acceleration in young supernova remnants.</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l40 level1 lfo80;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Map the intergalactic magnetic field strength by
measuring inverse Compton scattering of the cosmic microwave background from
relativistic electrons in AGN jets.</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l40 level1 lfo80;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Study chemical enrichment of galaxies through the
dispersion of nucleosynthesis elements by supernova explosions and stellar
winds.</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l40 level1 lfo80;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-size:10.0pt;
font-family:Symbol'><span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Investigate the formation and evolution of magnetic
dynamos in young and pre-main sequence stars buried deep in molecular clouds by
observing their X-ray coronal activity at high spectral resolution.<span
style='font-size:10.0pt'><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>Science requirements flow down directly from the above
Science Objectives and science goals, taken both individually and collectively,
to each of the Constellation-X technology areas. These technology areas are
primarily the optics and detectors, though the flowdown to all of the mission
technologies (including the ground segment) have been evaluated. Many of the
science flowdown requirements impact several technologies simultaneously. For
example, the first of the science objectives above is a requirement on high
sensitivity, which places simultaneous requirements on the telescope optics and
its associated detector(s). Many of the science requirements must also be placed
simultaneously on the optics and detectors, and take the interaction of the two
into account, and resulting in a system-level requirement. </p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>Below, we briefly present the science requirements for
each of the key technology areas.</p>

<h3><a name="_Toc7919084"></a><a name="_Toc7919451"></a><a name="_Toc7924640"></a><a
name="_Toc7972126"><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7924640'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919451'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919084'><![if !supportLists]>2.1.1<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Spectroscopy X-ray Telescope (SXT) Optics</span></span></span></a></h3>

<p class=MsoBodyText>There are three primary science driven requirements on the
SXT mirror system: effective area, angular resolution, and bandpass. These
requirements are developed in conjunction with presumed detector performance
and other telescope losses.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>X-ray throughput is the first primary requirement on the
SXT optics<a name="OLE_LINK1">, derived from Science Objectives I through IV</a>,
and is for high throughput, yielding at least 1000 counts in 10<span
style='mso-text-raise:1.5pt'>5</span> s for a flux of 2 x 10<span
style='mso-text-raise:1.5pt'>-15</span> ergs cm<span style='mso-text-raise:
1.5pt'>-2</span> s<span style='mso-text-raise:1.5pt'>-1</span>.<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>These requirements led to system
effective areas that have been specified at 0.25, 1.25, and 6.4 Kilo Electron
Volts (keV) of 1,000, 15,000 and 6,000 cm<sup>2</sup>, respectively.<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>This requirement must be implemented in
conjunction with an understanding of the quantum efficiency<b> </b><span
style='font-weight:normal'>(QE) of the detectors.<span style='color:red'><o:p></o:p></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>Angular (spatial) resolution is the second primary
requirement on the SXT optics, and derives equally from two different
requirements:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>spectral resolution
and flux sensitivity.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Again, these
are derived from considerations of Science Objectives I through IV.<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>First, the SXT optics must provide for
high spectral resolution from 0.25 to 10, which requires consideration of the
detector systems.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>While the
calorimeter provides the necessary spectral resolution independent of the
optics spatial resolution, the gratings place a requirement on the SXT optics
for spatial resolution to achieve the specified system minimum resolution
(R=300).<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Second, the spatial
resolution must also be adequate to avoid source confusion at the faint source
limit.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>These requirements yield a
spatial resolution requirement of 15 arc seconds Half Power Diameter (HPD)<span
style='color:blue'> </span>for the mission, which is consistent with 10 arc
seconds HPD for each SXT mirror</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The bandpass from 0.25 to 10 keV is developed by
consideration of the dual telescope system on Constellation: the SXT and Hard
X-ray Telescope (HXT) bandpasses must overlap to allow adequate
cross-calibration of the continuum x-ray fluxes.</p>

<h3><a name="_Toc7851589"></a><a name="_Toc7919085"></a><a name="_Toc7919452"></a><a
name="_Toc7924641"></a><a name="_Toc7972127"><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7924641'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919452'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919085'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7851589'><![if !supportLists]>2.1.2<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>X-ray Calorimeter</span></span></span></span></a></h3>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The primary science requirements that flow to the
calorimeter are for spectral resolution, bandpass, count rate and, in
conjunction with the SXT optics, field of view. </p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The X-ray calorimeter is a non-dispersive instrument, and
the top-level requirement for resolving power<span style='color:blue'> </span>is
R=3000 from 6  8.5 keV; i.e., 2 Electron Volt (eV) energy resolution.<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The minimum spectral resolution
anywhere over the line-rich 0.25  10 keV bandpass is set by the conditions
that 1) there be sufficient resolution to separate the important
density-sensitive He-like triplets (resonance, forbidden and intercombination
lines) arising from the O, N, Mg, Si and S ions and 2) the majority of the
individual spectral lines in this bandpass be resolved.<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>For the X-ray calorimeter in
particular, the spectral resolving power in the 6.0 8.5 keV bandpass must be
high enough to 1) distinguish the lithium-like satellite lines from the
overlapping helium-like transitions, and 2) achieve a velocity resolution of at
least 20 km s-1 in the Fe K lines.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>A minimum field of view of 2.5 arc minutes has been
specified to allow for studies of extended objects.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>In addition, the detector must critically sample the SXT
point response function.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The
combination of these requirements yields a requirement for at least a 30 x 30
pixel array.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>A bright source requirement imposes a count rate of 1,000
counts per second (cps) per pixel over 3x3 pixels or 10,000 cps over the
detector.</p>

<h3><a name="_Toc7851590"></a><a name="_Toc7919086"></a><a name="_Toc7919453"></a><a
name="_Toc7924642"></a><a name="_Toc7972128"><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7924642'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919453'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919086'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7851590'><![if !supportLists]>2.1.3<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Adiabatic Demagnetization Refrigerator (ADR</span>)</span></span></span></a></h3>

<p class=MsoBodyText>There are no direct science requirements that flow to the
ADR. The ADR requirements flow from the X-ray calorimeter requirements. Hence,
the ADR must provide adequate temperature control (absolute temperature and
temperature variations) that permits 2eV resolution in the calorimeter.<span
style='font-size:10.0pt'><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span></span>These
calorimeter science requirements result in engineering requirements on heat
rejection at the hot stage of the ADR, and tight control over the temperature
stability of 10 micro Kelvin (rms) at the cold stage. </p>

<h3><a name="_Toc7851591"></a><a name="_Toc7919087"></a><a name="_Toc7919454"></a><a
name="_Toc7924643"></a><a name="_Toc7972129"><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7924643'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919454'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919087'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7851591'><![if !supportLists]>2.1.4<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Cryocooler</span></span></span></span></a></h3>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The direct science requirements that flow to the
cryocooler are based on the required lifetime. Indirectly, the cryocooler requirements
derive from the ADR cooling requirements (which are in turn driven by the
calorimeter array size and the readout electronics).<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>The mission lifetime requirement has been set at a minimum
of 4 years of normal mission operations, with consumables sized for a minimum
of 6 years.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The array size is
driven by a science requirement on the calorimeter to provide a field of view
of at least 2.5 arc minutes with 5 arc seconds pixels (i.e., at least a 30x30
array).<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The readout electronics
and their heat loading is driven by the science requirement on the calorimeter
to allow for count rates of 1000 cps/pixel, or 10,000 cps averaged over the
detector array, on a single telescope. This flows down to a cryocooler with a
cooling capability of at least 7.5 milliwatts at 6K.</p>

<h3><a name="_Toc7851592"></a><a name="_Toc7919088"></a><a name="_Toc7919455"></a><a
name="_Toc7924644"></a><a name="_Toc7972130"><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7924644'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919455'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919088'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7851592'><![if !supportLists]>2.1.5<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Gratings and Charged Coupled Devices (CCDs</span>)</span></span></span></a></h3>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The science requirements that flow to the gratings and
CCDs need to be considered together, though because the technology developments
are substantially different, we consider them separately in the following
section. The key requirements are effective areas, energy resolution, and
bandpass.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The primary top level science requirement that flows to
the grating/CCD is, in combination with the SXT optics, to achieve specified
effective areas with a resolving power of R &gt; 300 from 0.25 to ~1keV. The
minimum spectral resolution anywhere over the line-rich 0.25  10 keV bandpass
is set by the conditions that 1) it be sufficient resolution to separate the
important density-sensitive He-like triplets (resonance, forbidden and
intercombination lines) arising from the O, N, Mg, Si and S ions, and 2) the
majority of the individual spectral lines in this bandpass be resolved, and
that a velocity resolution of &lt; 100km/sec can be achieved.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The second top level science requirement that flows to the
gratings is to cover the bandpass from 0.25 to ~1 keV.<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Use of gratings for the low end of the
bandpass follows from the fact that, for calorimeters<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>&#8710;E is constant, thus &#955;/<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>&#8710;&#955; falls linearly with energy and is insufficient
at energies less than ~0.6 keV.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>In
addition, the X-ray calorimeter efficiency is limited at low energies due to
the incorporation of long wavelength blocking filters.<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>For a dispersive spectrometer,
&#8710;&#955; is approximately constant, so <span lang=EN-GB style='font-family:
Symbol;color:black;mso-ansi-language:EN-GB'>l/Dl</span> <span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;</span>rises inversely with decreasing
energy.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>For reflection gratings,
the efficiency also increases at low energies due to increasing reflection
efficiency.</p>

<h3><a name="_Toc7851593"></a><a name="_Toc7919089"></a><a name="_Toc7919456"></a><a
name="_Toc7924645"></a><a name="_Toc7972131"><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7924645'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919456'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919089'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7851593'><![if !supportLists]>2.1.6<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Hard X-ray Telescope (HXT</span>)</span></span></span></a></h3>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The primary science requirements that flow to the HXT
(optics plus detectors) are bandpass, energy resolution, and sensitivity.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>A broad bandpass is required to address Science Objectives
I  IV. Many cosmic sources exhibit spectral features over a broad range of
energies. These include Active Galactic Nuclei (AGN), in which Compton
reflection off surrounding cold material produces a continuum spectrum at
energies above 10 keV; stellar flares, in which a hard, non-thermal impulsive
continuum above 10 keV can accompany the thermal emission produced during
coronal heating events below 2 keV; and Supernova Remnants (SNRs), in which the
synchrotron radiation generated by cosmic ray electrons accelerated at the
shock front can produce a high energy tail in addition to the thermal
component.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>At the high energy end,
the HXT must be capable of reaching 40 keV. The requirement at the low energy
end is set at 6 keV such that there is sufficient overlap with the calorimeter
to allow for cross-calibration of x-ray continuum spectra.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The energy resolution requirement derives from the ability
to determine the form of the X-ray spectrum above 10 keV. A requirement on the
energy resolution of &#916;E/E &lt;10% is adequate to achieve this goal, and
has been placed on the HXT, which is sufficient to characterize the continuum
emission.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The effective area requirement is set by the need for the
HXT system to provide a good S/N spectrum in the same time (10<sup>5</sup>
seconds) as the SXT observations of the faint sources noted in Science
Objective I.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>This places a
requirement of 1,500 cm<sup>2</sup> at 40 keV </p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>As with the SXT, the HXT angular resolution requirement is
set to allow confusion-limited observations of the faintest source populations
to be studied. For the harder X-ray sources, this requires a telescope HPD of 1
arc minute.</p>

<h2><a name="_Toc7837411"></a><a name="_Toc7846482"></a><a name="_Toc7851594"></a><a
name="_Toc7919090"></a><a name="_Toc7919457"></a><a name="_Toc7924646"></a><a
name="_Toc7972132"><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7924646'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919457'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919090'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7851594'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7846482'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7837411'><![if !supportLists]>2.2.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Spectroscopy X-ray Telescope (SXT) Optics</span></span></span></span></span></span></a></h2>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in;mso-list:l2 level1 lfo14'><![if !supportLists]>1.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What are the Level 1 and Level 2 science requirements for the
proposed mission, and how do these motivate the candidate technologies which
will be investigated?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Explain the
connections between the science requirements and the engineering requirements
on those technologies.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>There are four primary requirements on the SXT mirror
system.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Three are science driven,
and one is mission driven:</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='text-indent:0in'>Effective area - from the top
level flux sensitivity requirement, the SXT needs to provide sufficient
collecting area so the observatory collecting area for high resolution
spectroscopy meets or exceeds 15,000 cm^2 at 1.25 keV and 6,000 cm^2 at 6.4
keV.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Accounting for detector
quantum efficiency, the SXT mirror must provide 30,000 cm^2 at 1 keV and 7,500
cm^2 at 6.4 keV.</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='text-indent:0in'>Angular resolution - from the
top level flux sensitivity and spectral resolution requirement (in conjunction
with grating dispersion), the Half-Power Diameter (HPD) of the entire telescope
must be smaller than 15 arc seconds.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>The SXT mirror must provide an HPD better than 10 arc seconds.</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='text-indent:0in'>Bandpass - from the top level
science requirement, the SXT must have a band pass of 0.25-10 keV.<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span></p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='text-indent:0in'>Mass (mission driven) -
observing time requirement leads to the need for a high altitude orbit.<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>This in turn limits the spacecraft
mass. Given this spacecraft mass, four identical spacecraft are baselined to
meet the effective area requirement.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><u>Implementation</u>:<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>The Reference Configuration for Constellation-X entails four
identical spacecraft and sets of instrumentation.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>Each of the four identical SXT mirrors is a Wolter I grazing
incidence mirror with a 10 m focal length and a 1.6 m diameter.<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The mirror is composed of many
(100-250) nested Wolter 1 reflectors.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>The SXT optics utilizes a segmented approach.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>Instead of consisting of a complete surface of revolution,
each mirror will be constructed as a set of identical azimuthal segments.<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>In the current design concept,
reflectors with diameter smaller than 0.8 m will consist of 8 azimuthal
segments, and larger reflectors will consist of 16.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>The parabolic (primary) and hyperbolic (secondary)
reflectors will be constructed separately. Reflector segments are composed of thin
(0.4 mm) glass, thermally formed to the correct figure, and provided an X-ray
reflecting surface via epoxy replication from a precise mandrel.<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Reflectors within a module (an
azimuthal portion of the mirror) are aligned using a combination of optical means
and accurate metering via etched Si microstructures.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>2.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What are the significant technological challenges for these
technologies --- i.e., which technical capabilities have not already been
demonstrated?</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The fundamental challenge is constructing a mirror with
the required angular resolution.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>The other requirements - mass, bandpass, and collecting area - are
easily met by the current approach.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>A second challenge is establishing an approach for mass
production of reflectors and rapid accurate alignment of the reflectors within
a module.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>This challenge arises
from the Constellation-X development<span style='color:blue'> </span>time line
that requires completion of the SXT mirrors at an approximate rate of one per
year.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>3.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>For each technological challenge, what are the metrics by
which success --- i.e., technical readiness --- is to be measured?</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The metric for angular resolution is the half power
diameter in X-rays (10 arc seconds) of a mirror assembly.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The metrics for mass production is the rate at which
reflectors are produced, and the time necessary to assemble and align a module.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>4.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What kinds of demonstrations are required to validate
technical readiness? Will ground testing be sufficient, or are there technical
capabilities which can only be demonstrated in space?</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>Ground tests are sufficient for demonstrating the SXT
mirror performance. We will build a progression of prototype mirrors, each with
a more flight-like configuration than its predecessors.<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>For each of these, we will demonstrate
via X-ray test that HPD meets the mission requirement before and after
environmental tests.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>The first
such performance demonstration, for the Engineering Unit, should take place by
the end of 2003. </p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The phased development of the prototypes also provides a
means for developing and demonstrating of reflector mass production and module
alignment.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The mass production and
alignment approach should be demonstrated by the end of 2005.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>5.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What is status of each metric --- i.e., compare the current
capability with the required capability?</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The best segmented lightweight optical system that has
flownAstro-E, had angular resolution of ~100 arc second HPD. These mirrors
were fabricated using a far less precise approach.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>We have shown that most of the key components of a mirror
system meet their requirement (as specified in an error budget), and the
remainder are close.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>For instance,
the Si alignment bars meet their requirement for accuracy and repeatability,
and replication mandrels similar to those currently being fabricated have
exceeded the Constellation-X requirement.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>The figure of formed glass substrates is approaching the required
accuracy.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>We are assembling the
components into a module that will establish a baseline for system-level
angular resolution.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>We are also
addressing the optics development at the system level by developing the
assembly design.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>Process development is still underway for the mirror
components, reflector fabrication and alignment in particular.<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>As these are defined, it will be
possible to address the facility requirements for mass production, and the time
necessary for alignment.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>6.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Is the required capability a reasonable extension of the
current capability or does it require a significant advancement or new
approach?</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>While the angular resolution requirement for
Constellation-X is significantly better than that achieved with the previous
(Astro-E) approach, the groundwork had been laid for most of this advance, so
the required capability is now an extension of the existing approach.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The mass production and alignment will draw heavily from
the Astro-E approach, but will incorporate the different reflector fabrication
technique and a more accurate alignment approach.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The table below summarizes how the some of the component
fabrication and alignment technologies used for Astro-E mirrors are being
modified to meet the Constellation-X requirements.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]><span
style='font-style:normal'>7.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Is the specific technological challenge being addressed
for other applications?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Identify
technical<span style='font-style:normal'> </span>synergies with other NASA
programs if they exist.<span style='font-style:normal'><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The development of this large area, light weight X-ray
optics technology<span style='color:green'> </span>enables future X-ray
missions; e.g., XEUS and Generation-X. Thus, there is synergy with efforts in
other bands to produce lightweight optics (Large Telescope Space Initiative).</p>

<h2><a name="_Toc7837412"></a><a name="_Toc7846483"></a><a name="_Toc7851595"></a><a
name="_Toc7919091"></a><a name="_Toc7919458"></a><a name="_Toc7924647"></a><a
name="_Toc7972133"><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7924647'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919458'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919091'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7851595'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7846483'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7837412'><![if !supportLists]>2.3.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>X-ray Calorimeter</span></span></span></span></span></span></a></h2>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in;mso-list:l2 level1 lfo36'><![if !supportLists]>1.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What are the Level 1 and Level 2 science requirements for the
proposed mission, and how do these motivate the candidate technologies which
will be investigated?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Explain the
connections between the science requirements and the engineering requirements
on those technologies.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The requirements for energy resolution, high sensitivity,
maximal field of view and detector read out speed are traceable to the specific
scientific requirements of the mission<span style='color:blue'> </span>as
described in Section 2.1.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The
X-ray calorimeter provides the capability for high spectral and high quantum
efficiency over a large energy bandwidth, without degradation due to finite
source extent, and can deliver this resolution up to counting rates in the
100-1000 Hz range (with calculable dead time.)<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>This makes these devices an ideal choice for spectroscopy of
weak sources, including extended sources.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>2.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What are the significant technological challenges for these
technologies --- i.e., which technical capabilities have not already been
demonstrated?</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The detector array requirements for Constellation-X are
significantly more challenging than the performance characteristics of the
X-ray calorimeters currently in use.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>The key areas for technology development are a spectral resolution of
several eV out to ~ 8 keV, smaller pixels to allow appropriate matching to
improved mirror point spread functions, larger arrays (e.g., &gt; 30 x 30
elements) to subtend reasonable fields of view, and high spectral and quantum
efficiency uniformity over the array<span style='font-family:Arial;color:black'>.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><u>What's been demonstrated</u>:<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>An energy resolution of 2 eV at 1.5 keV and about 4-5 eV at
6 keV has been demonstrated on single pixel devices.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>This resolution has been achieved at counting rates of up to
a few hundred counts per second.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><u>What needs to be demonstrated</u><span
style='font-family:Arial;color:black'>: <o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='text-indent:0in'>Spectral resolutions of a few
eV on small arrays of simultaneously read out pixels.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>At present, the baseline pixel size for the Constellation-X
calorimeter array is 250 microns.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>This is traceable to a 15 arc second HPD X-ray point spread function and
assuming image over-sampling by a factor of three (i.e., 5 arc second pixels.)</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='text-indent:0in'>Demonstrate read out schemes
(either single string per pixel or multiplexed) that allow the full energy
resolution of the array to be realized and which can be extended to full array
sizes (e.g., up to 32 pixel columns or rows).<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>These must also be compatible with realizable dewar system
designs.</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='text-indent:0in'>Operate detectors at rates
approaching 1000 Hz and quantify dead time effects.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>3.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>For each technological challenge, what are the metrics by
which success --- i.e., technical readiness --- is to be measured?</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l36 level1 lfo79;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Pixel size (area and thickness necessary for high
quantum efficiency):<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>250 micron
pixels and &gt; 90% QE at 6 keV.</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l36 level1 lfo79;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Energy Resolution:<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>2 eV at 6 keV.</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l36 level1 lfo79;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Resolution uniformity:<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>Assuming a resolution of 2 eV, a uniformity of ~ 1 eV over
the array is desirable to allow co-adding of spectra from four arrays.</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l36 level1 lfo79;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Array filling factor.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>&gt; 95%.</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l36 level1 lfo79;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Robust fabrication process to ensure high yields for
four separate instruments, including spares and engineering models.</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l36 level1 lfo79;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Number of channels simultaneously read out.</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l36 level1 lfo79;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Detector Speed.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>Faster pulses obviously allow higher counting rates to be achieved with
lower dead time.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Since some amount
of dead time is unavoidable, a metric will be to quantify the dead time effects
at counting rates approaching 1 kHz, and devise pulse energy determination
algorithms that maximize throughput for different resolution grades.</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l36 level1 lfo79;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Scalability of system design to full-sized arrays of 32
x 32 pixels (i.e., detectors, amplifiers, and analog and digital electronics.)</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>4.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What kinds of demonstrations are required to validate
technical readiness? Will ground testing be sufficient, or are there technical
capabilities which can only be demonstrated in space?</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l7 level1 lfo78;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Operating arrays of devices that implement basic
requirements for pixel size, quantum efficiency, etc., simultaneously (e.g., 2
x 2 array).<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>This permits the
uniformity on small pixels to be assessed, as well as system issues (thermal
and electrical cross talk.)</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l7 level1 lfo78;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Read out small but meaningful subsets of pixels (e.g.,
4 x 4 or 2 x 8) to demonstrate viability of read out schemes, including
multiplexed schemes.</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l7 level1 lfo78;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Demonstrate 3 x 32 calorimeter channels operated simultaneously.</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l7 level1 lfo78;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Operate these systems in real-world low temperature
systems (in particular ADRs, with their associated magnetic fields.)</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l7 level1 lfo78;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Demonstrate that detector read out schemes produce heat
loads compatible with likely cooling techniques.</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l7 level1 lfo78;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Demonstrate that detector technology and read out
scheme are robust with respect to cosmic rays.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>This includes both radiation damage and radiation affect on
detector performance (energy resolution and dead time effects.)<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>This can be assessed to a large extent
from ground tests, but simulating cosmic ray effects is difficult and nothing
can compare with in-flight experience.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>Ground laboratory testing and subsequent environmental
testing of near flight-like configurations are all that is required to
demonstrate technology readiness.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>No space-based demonstrator is required.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>5.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What is status of each metric --- i.e., compare the current
capability with the required capability?</p>

  <p class=MsoNormal><span style='font-size:9.0pt;color:black'>2 eV up to ~ 8

  <td width=131 style='width:130.5pt;border-top:none;border-left:none;

  <p class=MsoNormal><span style='font-size:9.0pt;color:black'>4-5 eV at 6 keV<o:p></o:p></span></p>

  <td width=131 style='width:130.5pt;border:solid windowtext .5pt;border-top:
