  height:.2in'>
  <p class=MsoNormal><span style='font-size:9.0pt;color:black'>Pulse time
  constant<o:p></o:p></span></p>
  </td>
  <td width=131 style='width:130.5pt;border-top:none;border-left:none;
  border-bottom:solid windowtext .5pt;border-right:solid windowtext .5pt;
  mso-border-top-alt:solid windowtext .5pt;mso-border-left-alt:solid windowtext .5pt;
  padding:0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;height:.2in'>
  <p class=MsoNormal><span style='font-size:9.0pt;color:black'>100-500
  microsecond<o:p></o:p></span></p>
  </td>
  <td width=131 style='width:130.5pt;border-top:none;border-left:none;
  border-bottom:solid windowtext .5pt;border-right:solid windowtext .5pt;
  mso-border-top-alt:solid windowtext .5pt;mso-border-left-alt:solid windowtext .5pt;
  padding:0in 5.4pt 0in 5.4pt;height:.2in'>
  <p class=MsoNormal><span style='font-size:9.0pt;color:black'>&gt; 300
  microsecond<o:p></o:p></span></p>
  </td>
 </tr>
</table>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>6.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Is the required capability a reasonable extension of the
current capability or does it require a significant advancement or new
approach?</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>There are two X-ray calorimeter technologies being
supported by Constellation-X Research and Development (R&amp;D) funding.<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>These are devices with superconducting
transition edge thermometers and doped semiconductor thermometers.<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Based on the promising single pixel
results that have been obtained so far, the prospects for achieving the goals
of Constellation-X should eventually be possible without fundamental
breakthroughs.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>However, reaching
the necessary level of technology readiness [i.e., Technology Readiness Level
(TRL)-6] by the middle of this decade will require many areas of technology
development to be carried out in parallel.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>To achieve the goals of the Constellation-X mission, both
technologies require significant advancement in order to demonstrate the flight
readiness of each approach.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><u>Thermometer</u>:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>For semiconductor thermometers, characterize thermometer responsivity
with geometry, implant dose, etc.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>For the transition edge sensor (TES) devices, develop robust fabrication
process for repeatable transition temperature, Tc, sufficient critical current,
etc.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Evaluate performance on
thermometer sizes required for 250 micron unit cells.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><u>Noise sources</u>:<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>Both thermometer types exhibit a certain amount of noise in
excess of simple phonon and Johnson noise.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>Determine how noise scales with device parameters by
fabricating test devices to map out the noise dependence.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><u>Absorbers</u>:</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>For semiconductor devices, develop process for attaching
Sn foil and dicing (e.g., by laser) to create uniform absorber size and
spacing.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>For TES, develop process
for directly depositing absorbers onto TES.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>Demonstrate high spectral resolution up to ~8 keV.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><u>System:<o:p></o:p></u></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:.75in;text-indent:-.25in;mso-list:l41 level1 lfo77;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Evaluate thermal and electrical cross talk using small
arrays.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:.75in;text-indent:-.25in;mso-list:l41 level1 lfo77;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Assess system issues (thermal and mechanical) for
implementing very large numbers of Junction Field Effect Transistors (JFETs)
(running at up to 130K for minimum noise) and Superconducting Quantum Interface
Device (SQUIDs).</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:.75in;text-indent:-.25in;mso-list:l41 level1 lfo77;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Develop Transition Edge Sensor (TES)/SQUID interface
for 1000 pixel array.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:.75in;text-indent:-.25in;mso-list:l41 level1 lfo77;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Develop multiplex chip and control electronics,
including MUX design and layout, optimizing for speed, noise, power, and number
of channels to MUX (32 or fewer?), etc.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:.75in;text-indent:-.25in;mso-list:l41 level1 lfo77;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Develop digital signal processor system capable of
handling 1000 pixel arrays within very tight power constraints.<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>This is required for either sensor
type.<i><o:p></o:p></i></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:.75in;text-indent:-.25in;mso-list:l41 level1 lfo77;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Carry out radiation hardness tests of JFETs and SQUIDs</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:.75in;text-indent:-.25in;mso-list:l41 level1 lfo77;
tab-stops:list .75in'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:Symbol'><span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Design anticoincidence detector appropriate for each
type of sensor.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>7.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Is the specific technological challenge being addressed for
other applications?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Identify
technical synergies with other NASA programs if they exist.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>To a large extent, the read out of large arrays of X-ray
calorimeters is being paralleled in the development of large IR and mm-wave
bolometer arrays for both ground-based and space-borne observatories.<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Many of the issues are the same, such
as thermometer technology, detector mounting and interfaces to amplifiers
(JFETs and SQUIDs).<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>But there are
very significant differences.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The
X-ray devices must be much faster in order to detect individual photons up to
relatively high counting rates.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>They require thick absorbers to provide high quantum efficiency up to 8
keV or so.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>These absorbers must
have a particular heat capacity, thermalize photons with high uniformity, and
be compatible with the full fabrication process.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>The read out of these sensor technologies is indeed
synergistic, but again, the higher speeds of the X-ray sensors requires specialized
development of the detectors all the way out to the digital read out
electronics.</p>

<h2><a name="_Toc7511958"></a><a name="_Toc7514611"></a><a name="_Toc7593042"></a><a
name="_Toc7593130"></a><a name="_Toc7837413"></a><a name="_Toc7846484"></a><a
name="_Toc7851596"></a><a name="_Toc7919092"></a><a name="_Toc7919459"></a><a
name="_Toc7924648"></a><a name="_Toc7972134"><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7924648'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919459'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919092'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7851596'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7846484'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7837413'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593130'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593042'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514611'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511958'><![if !supportLists]>2.4.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Adiabatic Demagnetization Refrigerator (ADR)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593130'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593042'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514611'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511958'></span></span></span></span></h2>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='margin-left:.5in;text-indent:-.25in;mso-list:
l12 level1 lfo74'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593130'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593042'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514611'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511958'><![if !supportLists]>1.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What are the Level 1 and Level 2 science requirements for the
proposed mission, and how do these motivate the candidate technologies which
will be investigated?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Explain the
connections between the science requirements and the engineering requirements
on those technologies.</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593130'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593042'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514611'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511958'>The 2eV calorimeter requires subKelvin, stable
operational temperatures.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>ADR
technology has been baselined to provide the calorimeter operational temperature.
The hot end of ADR must interface with a 6K cryocooler. </span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='margin-left:.5in;text-indent:-.25in;mso-list:
l12 level1 lfo74'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593130'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593042'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514611'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511958'><![if !supportLists]>2.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What are the significant technological challenges for these
technologies --- i.e., which technical capabilities have not already been
demonstrated?</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593130'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593042'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514611'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511958'>A flight qualified ADR with an operational
temperature of 50 mK and hot end of 1 K has been developed for ASTRO-E. Finer
cold end temperature stability, higher temperature hot end, and higher cooling
capacity are required for the Constellation-X ADR. </span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593130'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593042'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514611'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511958'>Several Constellation-X ADR technical challenges
have already been overcome and demonstrated by a three-stage laboratory model
ADR. This model demonstrated the required cold end temperature and stability in
a continuously operating system</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593130'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593042'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514611'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511958'>The primary remaining technical challenge for
the ADR is demonstration of the hot end stage(s), which extends from 1-2 K to
6K. The hot ADR stages require new magnets, power leads, magnet electronics,
salt pills and integration materials.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>The subsequent remaining challenge will be integration of these stages
with the proven 50mK to 1-2K stages into a system that meets the overall
performance.</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='margin-left:.5in;text-indent:-.25in;mso-list:
l12 level1 lfo74'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593130'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593042'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514611'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511958'><![if !supportLists]>3.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>For each technological challenge, what are the metrics by
which success --- i.e., technical readiness --- is to be measured?</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyTextIndent3><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593130'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593042'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514611'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511958'>The primary metrics to achieve are a hot end
temperature of 6K and overall system cooling capacity of 5 microwatts while
maintaining the cold end temperature of 50 mK and stability of 10 microKelvin
(rms). The cold end temperature and stability have already been demonstrated.</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='margin-left:.5in;text-indent:-.25in;mso-list:
l12 level1 lfo74'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593130'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593042'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514611'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511958'><![if !supportLists]>4.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What kinds of demonstrations are required to validate
technical readiness? Will ground testing be sufficient, or are there technical
capabilities which can only be demonstrated in space?</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593130'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593042'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514611'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511958'>Ground testing in the relevant thermal vacuum
and launch vibration environments is sufficient to demonstrate the ADR
technology.</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593130'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593042'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514611'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511958'>ADR technology has been baselined over the
dilution refrigerator technology because the latter requires on-orbit (or other
zero g) demonstration. <s><o:p></o:p></s></span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='margin-left:.5in;text-indent:-.25in;mso-list:
l12 level1 lfo74'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593130'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593042'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514611'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511958'><![if !supportLists]>5.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What is status of each metric --- i.e., compare the current
capability with the required capability?</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593130'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593042'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514611'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511958'>Temperature control has been demonstrated to a
level of 8 microKelvin (rms) at 50 mK by a three stage ADR with a hot end of
1-2 K and continuous cooling at the cold end. This meets the requirement of the
first three stages. Additional stage(s) will extend the hot end to 6K. </span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593130'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593042'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514611'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511958'>The final stages require new refrigerant,
magnets, and lead materials that function at 2 to 6K. Candidate materials are
currently under investigation. A laboratory model of final stage going up to
4.5K liquid Helium temperature is expected to be completed by the end of Fiscal
Year 2002.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The next major
development will be to integrate all stages going up to 6K and demonstrate the
full system cooling by early Fiscal Year 2004. Finally, an engineering unit of
the multistage ADR will be built for performance and environmental testing by
the end of Fiscal Year 2006.</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='margin-left:.5in;text-indent:-.25in;mso-list:
l12 level1 lfo74'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593130'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593042'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514611'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511958'><![if !supportLists]>6.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Is the required capability a reasonable extension of the
current capability or does it require a significant advancement or new
approach?</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593130'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593042'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514611'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511958'>In all areas, the required capability can be
obtained as a reasonable extension of existing capabilities.&nbsp; </span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593130'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593042'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514611'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511958'>At a minimum, research is already underway
that has shown a probable solution in each case.&nbsp; In the case of producing
refrigerant materials in crystalline form, the capability to produce some
materials of interest can be revived by funding.<b><o:p></o:p></b></span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='margin-left:.5in;text-indent:-.25in;mso-list:
l12 level1 lfo74'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593130'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593042'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514611'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511958'><![if !supportLists]>7.<span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Is the specific technological challenge being addressed for
other applications?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Identify
technical synergies with other NASA programs if they exist.</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593130'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593042'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514611'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511958'>Cross Enterprise Technology Development
Program (CETDP) and Commercial Technology Development (CTD) NASA offices are
addressing the ADR development challenge for Constellation-X,<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>SPIRIT,<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>Sub millimeter Probe of the Evolution of Cosmic Structure
(SPECS), Filled Aperture Infrared Telescope (FAIR), Sub millimeter and Far
Infrared Experiment (SAFIRE), Space Ultraviolet Optical Observatory (SUVO),
Extreme Ultra Violet (EUV) Solar and Microarcsecond X-ray Imaging Mission
(MAXIM) applications.</span></span></span></span></p>

<h2><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593130'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593042'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514611'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511958'><a
name="_Toc7837414"></a><a name="_Toc7846485"></a><a name="_Toc7851597"></a><a
name="_Toc7919093"></a><a name="_Toc7919460"></a><a name="_Toc7924649"></a><a
name="_Toc7972135"><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7924649'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919460'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919093'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7851597'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7846485'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7837414'><![if !supportLists]>2.5.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Cryocooler</span></span></span></span></span></span></a></span></span></span></span></h2>

<span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511958'></span><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514611'></span><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593042'></span><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593130'></span>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in;mso-list:l2 level1 lfo68'><![if !supportLists]>1.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What are the Level 1 and Level 2 science requirements for the
proposed mission, and how do these motivate the candidate technologies which
will be investigated?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Explain the
connections between the science requirements and the engineering requirements
on those technologies.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The ADR cooling needs and long mission life requirements
motivate the cryocooler technology development. Mission requirements that flow
down to the cryocooler include a mass and power budget.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>2.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What are the significant technological challenges for these
technologies --- i.e., which technical capabilities have not already been
demonstrated?</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The most significant technological challenge is to reach a
cold end temperature of 6 K with sufficient cooling power to lift the ADR heat
load.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The ADR cooling needs may be met by stored expendable
cryogen systems that have limited life when cryogen mass is limited. This is
the case for many space applications due to limited launch mass.<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>To increase the life of <span
style='color:green'>future </span>space missions NASA JPL is leading a common
cryocooler technology development known as the Advanced Cryocooler Technology
Development Program (ACTDP), which encompasses the requirements for
Constellation-X, Next Generation Space Telescope (NGST) and Terrestrial Planet
Finder (TPF).</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>Four contractors are currently participating in the ACTDP
Study Phase, which will be followed by a Demonstration Phase to develop
prototype units of two or three technologies. The technologies currently under
contract are Multistage Pulse Tube System, Multi-Stage Proprietary TRW
Cryocooler, Joule Thomson (J-T) Cooler with 3-Stage Stirling Pre-cooler, and
Turbo-Brayton. Cryocooler.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The 6K cooling challenge is common to all projects.<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Also, there is an intermediate stage
cooling requirement for the other projects of which Constellation-X will be
taking advantage.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The temperature
of the intermediate stage cooling is 18K at 250 mW.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>3.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>For each technological challenge, what are the metrics by
which success --- i.e., technical readiness --- is to be measured?</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The metric is to lift 7.5 milliwatt (mW) heat load at 6 K
and 250 mW at 18 K for less than 150 W beginning-of-life input power and 40
Kilograms of mass.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>Reaching a temperature of 6K is a big challenge.<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Providing the cooling powers at 6K and
18K requires good staging and good performance.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>The thermodynamic efficiency also influences the required
input power.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>4.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What kinds of demonstrations are required to validate
technical readiness? Will ground testing be sufficient, or are there technical
capabilities which can only be demonstrated in space?</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>A cryocooler system (cooler with Bread Board electronics)
ground test demonstrating the 7.5 mW requirement will be completed and reported
on by each of 2 or 3 ACTDP contractors by mid 2005.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>An Engineering Model capable of withstanding launch and
flight environments will be tested on the ground in 2006 to demonstrate the
readiness of technology for Constellation-X flight. Ground testing will be
sufficient; there is no requirement for space demonstration.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>5.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What is status of each metric --- i.e., compare the current
capability with the required capability?</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The proof of concept Multi-Stage Pulse Tube Technology has
demonstrated less than 7K of cooling temperature with a mass of 26 Kilograms
and power of 106 Watts.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Others
have yet to attain the low temperature.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>The intermediate stage is also not demonstrated yet. Current
off-the-shelf capabilities for space borne cryocoolers are in the 30+ K
temperature region, but several <a name="OLE_LINK2">R&amp;D</a> efforts such as
Multistage Pulse Tube and Stirling have attained (with varying degrees of
qualification) cooling in the 10 K region.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>6.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Is the required capability a reasonable extension of the
current capability or does it require a significant advancement or new
approach?</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The required capability is the reasonable extension of the
current capability as each of the four contractors selected for the Study Phase
have proposed a varied mixture of existing technology and next-step technology
that is coming out of Internal Research and Development, SBIR or other funded
work.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>7.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Is the specific technological challenge being addressed for
other applications?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Identify
technical synergies with other NASA programs if they exist.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The ACTDP has active participation in setting
requirements, program reviews and contractor selection from Constellation-X,
NGST and TPF. </p>

<h2><a name="_Toc7511960"></a><a name="_Toc7514613"></a><a name="_Toc7593044"></a><a
name="_Toc7593132"></a><a name="_Toc7837415"></a><a name="_Toc7846486"></a><a
name="_Toc7851598"></a><a name="_Toc7919094"></a><a name="_Toc7919461"></a><a
name="_Toc7924650"></a><a name="_Toc7972136"><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7924650'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919461'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919094'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7851598'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7846486'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7837415'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593132'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593044'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514613'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511960'><![if !supportLists]>2.6.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Gratings</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></h2>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in;mso-list:l2 level1 lfo66'><a
name="_Toc7511962"></a><a name="_Toc7514615"></a><a name="_Toc7593046"></a><a
name="_Toc7593134"><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><![if !supportLists]>1.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What are the Level 1 and Level 2 science requirements for the
proposed mission, and how do these motivate the candidate technologies which
will be investigated?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Explain the
connections between the science requirements and the engineering requirements
on those technologies.</span></span></span></a></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>The top level science requirement that flows
to the gratings is, in combination with the CCD detector, to achieve specified
effective areas (&gt;1000cm<sup>2</sup>) with a resolving power of R &gt; 300
from 0.25 to ~1keV assuming 10 arc second HPD optics.</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>Mission requirements that flow down to the
gratings include a mass budget.</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in;mso-list:l2 level1 lfo7'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><![if !supportLists]>2.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What are the significant technological challenges for these
technologies --- i.e., which technical capabilities have not already been
demonstrated?</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>The baseline technology for the Constellation-X
gratings is a reflection grating that is an evolution of the design flown on
XMM. </span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>The key challenge for this approach is to
develop grating substrates with the required groove efficiency while meeting
the required mass density per unit area and required optical tolerances. Master
gratings that meet Constellation-X requirements have been fabricated.
Micro-roughness of blazed facets with photolithographic process on silicon is
below 0.4 nm (compared to XMM: ~ 1.2 nm), and diffraction efficiency is
excellent.</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>An alternate approach is an off-plane radial
groove grating. The technological challenge to this approach is to achieve
adequate groove efficiencies at the required ruling density and with the proper
radial groove geometry and blaze angle, while maintaining adequate optical
tolerances.</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>The technology to fabricate the grating master
is the primary challenge for this alternate approach. However, it potentially
offers advantages in terms of science enhancement as well as easing the fabrication
requirements on the grating substrates. This approach requires exploration of
several aspects to be compared with the baseline approach: </span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l17 level1 lfo75;
tab-stops:list .75in'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:
Symbol'><span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Optical tolerances on the substrates</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l17 level1 lfo75;
tab-stops:list .75in'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:
Symbol'><span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Assembly and alignment tolerances;</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l17 level1 lfo75;
tab-stops:list .75in'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:
Symbol'><span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Spectral resolution;</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l17 level1 lfo75;
tab-stops:list .75in'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:
Symbol'><span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Ruling densities;</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l17 level1 lfo75;
tab-stops:list .75in'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:
Symbol'><span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Groove efficiencies and the total number of gratings;</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in;mso-list:l2 level1 lfo7'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><![if !supportLists]>3.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>For each technological challenge, what are the metrics by
which success --- i.e., technical readiness --- is to be measured?</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>The driving metrics for the reflection
gratings are:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span></span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l34 level1 lfo76;
tab-stops:list .75in'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:
Symbol'><span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Substrate mass per unit area<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><u>&lt;</u> 0.2 g/cm </span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l34 level1 lfo76;
tab-stops:list .75in'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:
Symbol'><span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Substrate flatness &lt; 0.5 micro m</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText style='margin-left:.75in;text-indent:-.25in;mso-list:l34 level1 lfo76;
tab-stops:list .75in'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:
Symbol'><span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>The driving metrics for the off-plane radial groove
gratings are:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span></span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='text-indent:0in'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>Groove efficiency in radial groove geometry of
25%<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span></span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='text-indent:0in'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>The substrate mass and flatness, and assembly
tolerances would be relaxed for the off-plane grating approach in comparison
with the baseline.</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in;mso-list:l2 level1 lfo7'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><![if !supportLists]>4.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What kinds of demonstrations are required to validate
technical readiness? Will ground testing be sufficient, or are there technical
capabilities which can only be demonstrated in space?</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>Laboratory demonstrations and subsequent
environmental testing of near flight-like configurations of the gratings are
all that is required for either the baseline or the alternate approach. No
space-based demonstrator is required.</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in;mso-list:l2 level1 lfo7'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><![if !supportLists]>5.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What is status of each metric --- i.e., compare the current
capability with the required capability?</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>Minimal funding has been devoted so far to the
baseline approach. Accomplishments against the metrics listed above include:</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='text-indent:0in'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>Flatness of &lt;1 micron on a 100 mm diameter
wafer that meets the 0.2g/cm2 areal density requirement has been demonstrated
with magneto-rheological figuring (MRF).</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>For the alternative approach: Plans are in
place, but no hardware has been fabricated. A grant is in place to assess
feasibility and generate specifications for holographic recording geometry by
late FY 2002. A holographic grating with 5500 g/mm with the a parallel groove
configuration at 30 degree blaze on a 58 mm x 58 mm (half size) substrate will
be produced by start of CY 2003. Laboratory evaluation of grating performance
follows prior to following step. Generation of a flight size 120mm square
grating with &gt;5500g/mm in a radial groove configuration will take place by
summer 2003, followed by laboratory evaluation of the grating later that year.</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in;mso-list:l2 level1 lfo7'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><![if !supportLists]>6.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Is the required capability a reasonable extension of the
current capability or does it require a significant advancement or new
approach?</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>The required capabilities for the baseline
approach are reasonable extensions of current grating fabrication techniques.
The gratings will be directly fabricated using interference lithography on
graze-cut silicon wafers. If a replication process is chosen instead,
extrapolating from XMM/Newton Reflection Grating Spectrometer experience, high
fidelity grating replication from a single master may require production of 7<sup>th</sup>
generation replicas in a complex replication tree. A uniform ruling density
master (38mm diameter) was fabricated and tested to provide proof of concept
and verification of groove efficiency for the anisotropically etched gratings
with flat, smooth facets Si(111) plane orientation. Extrapolation to include a
radial groove on a large size wafer<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>(200mm) appears to be reasonable extension of current technology.</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>The required capabilities for the alternate
approach require improvements in ruling techniques to simultaneously achieve
the groove density, groove geometry and groove efficiency. High density, blazed
gratings have been fabricated for use in deep UV, e.g. for COS on Hubble Space
Telescope (HST). Change of ruling geometry and evaluation of x-ray performance
is required, but no new technology. Off-plane geometry allows higher separation
between gratings so substrates may be thicker, which makes it easier to achieve
the required flatness. Standard thin plate replication technology may be
employed, but needs demonstration with holographic master gratings. This
alternate approach may also allow the mass constraints to be met without
significant technological advance, and should require fewer gratings to be
manufactured (perhaps by a factor of 2).</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in;mso-list:l2 level1 lfo7'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><![if !supportLists]>7.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Is the specific technological challenge being addressed for
other applications?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Identify
technical synergies with other NASA programs if they exist.</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>Lightweight gratings and flat substrates are
of use to many programs. Holographic high ruling density aberration-corrected
gratings in use for COS and for future UV missions such as SUVO.</span></span></span></span></p>

<h2><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><a
name="_Toc7511961"></a><a name="_Toc7514614"></a><a name="_Toc7593045"></a><a
name="_Toc7593133"></a><a name="_Toc7919095"></a><a name="_Toc7919462"></a><a
name="_Toc7924651"></a><a name="_Toc7972137"><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7924651'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919462'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919095'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593133'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593045'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514614'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511961'><![if !supportLists]>2.7.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Charge Coupled Device (CCD)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></span></span></span></span></h2>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in;mso-list:l2 level1 lfo67'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><![if !supportLists]>1.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What are the Level 1 and Level 2 science requirements for the
proposed mission, and how do these motivate the candidate technologies which
will be investigated?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Explain the
connections between the science requirements and the engineering requirements
on those technologies.</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>The key science driver for the CCD is, in
conjunction with the gratings, to obtain the required effective area at a
resolving power &gt;300 from 0.25 to ~1keV. Energy resolution in the CCD is
required to separate grating orders. CCD pixel sizes are driven by the required
spectral resolution.</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>Additional mission requirements that flow to
the CCDs are low power, radiation tolerance, high production yield and a mass
budget. </span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in;mso-list:l2 level1 lfo7'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><![if !supportLists]>2.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What are the significant technological challenges for these
technologies --- i.e., which technical capabilities have not already been
demonstrated?</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>The baseline technology for the Constellation-X
CCDs is a Resistive Gate CCD (RGCCD) approach that promises a low power,
radiation resistant device. The significant technological challenge is to
develop and prove the concept of the resistive gate structure. <span
style='color:maroon'><o:p></o:p></span></span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>An alternate approach to the CCD is an Event-Driven
CCD (EDCCD). This approach has a number of potentially attractive aspects
compared to the baseline approach: </span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l21 level1 lfo81;
tab-stops:list .75in'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:
Symbol'><span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Significant reduction in the power required for the
devices</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l21 level1 lfo81;
tab-stops:list .75in'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:
Symbol'><span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>High frame rate which will enhance the science return
and could<span style='color:#003300'> </span>relax the spacecraft stability and
jitter requirements, and reduce the optical stray light requirement by at least
and order of magnitude</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l21 level1 lfo81;
tab-stops:list .75in'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:
Symbol'><span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Reduced pile-up concerns</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l21 level1 lfo81;
tab-stops:list .75in'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:
Symbol'><span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Reduce the data volume that must be transferred to the
ground</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l21 level1 lfo81;
tab-stops:list .75in'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><![if !supportLists]><span style='font-family:
Symbol'><span style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><![endif]>Low power and the associated reduction mass savings on
the spacecraft</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>The primary technological challenges are to
develop the readout system for the EDCCD and to verify the Molecular Beam
Epitaxy (MBE) back-side treatment process. The pixel array technology remains
unchanged from existing CCDs. The MBE back-side treatment process will provide
the improved low energy response of the CCDs below 0.5 keV. Studies of the MBE
process are decoupled from the EDCCD geometry and electronics, and can occur in
parallel. The demonstrated yield of the MBE process is already at least an
order of magnitude above that used to provide the ACIS CCDs on Chandra. </span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>A recommendation is being considered by the
project to baseline the EDCCDs.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>The top level technology development roadmap and associated costs are
needed before this decision will be made.</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in;mso-list:l2 level1 lfo7'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span

</span><![endif]>For each technological challenge, what are the metrics by
which success --- i.e., technical readiness --- is to be measured?</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l19 level1 lfo82;

</span></span><![endif]>Frame rate<span style='mso-tab-count:1'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>10
Hz </span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l19 level1 lfo82;

times less than current devices</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l19 level1 lfo82;

</span></span><![endif]>QE:<span style='mso-tab-count:2'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>25%
at 0.25 keV</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l19 level1 lfo82;

</span></span><![endif]>Radiation hardness: 5x greater than Chandra ACIS CCDs</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l23 level1 lfo83;

</span></span><![endif]>Frame rate:<span style='mso-tab-count:1'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>&gt;
50 Hz</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l23 level1 lfo83;

</span></span><![endif]>Power:<span style='mso-tab-count:1'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>50

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l23 level1 lfo83;

</span></span><![endif]>QE:<span style='mso-tab-count:2'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>75%
at 0.25 keV</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='margin-left:.75in;mso-list:l23 level1 lfo83;

</span></span><![endif]>Radiation hardness: 10x greater than Chandra ACIS CCDs</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>Relatively high fabrication yield will be
required by either technology to support production of the large number of
CCD's required for the mission.</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in;mso-list:l2 level1 lfo7'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><![if !supportLists]>4.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What kinds of demonstrations are required to validate
technical readiness? Will ground testing be sufficient, or are there technical
capabilities which can only be demonstrated in space?</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>Laboratory demonstrations and subsequent
environmental testing of near flight-like configurations of the CCDs are all
that is required for either the baseline or the alternate approach. No space-based
demonstrator is required.</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in;mso-list:l2 level1 lfo7'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><![if !supportLists]>5.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What is status of each metric --- i.e., compare the current
capability with the required capability?</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>The current technology is defined by the
Chandra ACIS CCDs.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The back
illuminated devices have a QE at 0.25 keV of 25%, while the front illuminated
devices only have a QE ~1% at 0.25 keV. The Chandra CCDs have a frame rate of
0.3Hz. The power requirements and radiation hardness of the Chandra devices are
taken as unity for comparison purposes with the RGCCD or EDCCD metrics.</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>No work is currently being funded on the
RGCCDs. A single test lot was funded and fabricated in 1998.<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Basic functionality was demonstrated.<b><o:p></o:p></b></span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>For the EDCCD approach, fabrication of the
first set of devices began in February 2002, with completion planned for July
2002. This work is funded by internal MIT funds, and NASA ROSS2000. Device
packaging and preliminary screening is planned for August 2002. Plans for FY
2003 include a run with a fully depleted, thinned CCD with high QE at 150eV.</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in;mso-list:l2 level1 lfo7'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><![if !supportLists]>6.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Is the required capability a reasonable extension of the
current capability or does it require a significant advancement or new
approach?</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>While the RGCCDs required capabilities
represents a new type of CCD, they are based on well-understood CCD fabrication
techniques, and the first lot showed that the principle behind the RGCCD is
sound.<b><o:p></o:p></b></span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>The required capabilities for the EDCCD
approach are straightforward extensions of current CCD fabrication techniques.
The basic MBE process exists, and functioning devices with good X-ray energy
resolution and low energy response have been fabricated.</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in;mso-list:l2 level1 lfo7'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><![if !supportLists]>7.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Is the specific technological challenge being addressed for
other applications?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Identify
technical synergies with other NASA programs if they exist.</span></span></span></span></p>

<p class=MsoBodyText><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'>EDCCDs are suited for surface inspections, contamination
studies, and X-ray fluorescence studies for laboratory diagnostics; they are
also suitable for use in large coded aperture systems.<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Many applications exist in general
astronomy missions for high frame rate, radiation tolerant and low power CCDs.</span></span></span></span></p>

<h2><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593134'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593046'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514615'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511962'><a
name="_Toc7837417"></a><a name="_Toc7846488"></a><a name="_Toc7851600"></a><a
name="_Toc7919096"></a><a name="_Toc7919463"></a><a name="_Toc7924652"></a><a
name="_Toc7972138"><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7924652'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919463'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919096'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7851600'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7846488'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7837417'><![if !supportLists]>2.8.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Hard X-ray Telescope (HXT) Optics</span></span></span></span></span></span></a></span></span></span></span></h2>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in;mso-list:l2 level1 lfo64'><![if !supportLists]>1.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What are the Level 1 and Level 2 science requirements for the
proposed mission, and how do these motivate the candidate technologies which
will be investigated?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Explain the
connections between the science requirements and the engineering requirements
on those technologies.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The primary science requirements that flow to the HXT
optics are broad bandpass, spatial resolution, and sensitivity, as defined in
section 2.1.6.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>Additional mission requirements that flow to the HXT optics
include a mass budget.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>2.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What are the significant technological challenges for these
technologies --- i.e., which technical capabilities have not already been
demonstrated?</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='text-indent:0in'>The challenge is to demonstrate
subarcminute angular resolution for low-mass, high-reflectance
multilayer-coated optics.</p>

<p class=bodytextindent style='margin-left:.25in'>To date, prototype multilayer
mirrors have been fabricated which meet the reflectance requirement up to 50
keV using formed glass.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The
resolution must be improved and a full-sized flight prototype fabricated and tested.<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Replica Nickel optics have achieved the
desired resolution, but multilayers have not been fabricated on the interiors
of small-diameter shells.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>3.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>For each technological challenge, what are the metrics by
which success --- i.e., technical readiness --- is to be measured?</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='text-indent:0in'>Technical readiness will be
demonstrated by measuring the X-ray performance of a prototype optic consisting
of at least 10 full shells.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The
measurement must demonstrate the reflectance at 10, 30, and 50 keV, and must
show the angular resolution is less than 1 arc minute HPD.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>4.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What kinds of demonstrations are required to validate
technical readiness? Will ground testing be sufficient, or are there technical
capabilities which can only be demonstrated in space?</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='text-indent:0in'>Laboratory measurements of
reflectance and resolution.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>5.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What is status of each metric --- i.e., compare the current
capability with the required capability?</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='text-indent:0in'>The current capability:</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='text-indent:0in'>Glass optics: HPD 90 arc
seconds, reflectance &gt;45% to E=50 keV, can meet mass requirement.</p>

<p class=bodytextindent style='margin-left:.25in'>Ni replica: single thin
(low-mass) shells can be fabricated with &lt;60 arc second resolution but
multilayers have not been applied, so the reflectance has not been
demonstrated.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>6.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Is the required capability a reasonable extension of the
current capability or does it require a significant advancement or new
approach?</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The critical technologies are reasonable extensions of
existing technologies, as described above.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>7.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Is the specific technological challenge being addressed for
other applications?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Identify
technical synergies with other NASA programs if they exist.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>There is significant synergy with a number of balloon
SR&amp;T programs (HEFT, InFocus), with explorer concepts.<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>There is overlap with some balloon
programs but none are driving the requirements in this way.</p>

<h2 style='mso-list:l35 level2 lfo27'><a name="_Toc7511963"></a><a
name="_Toc7514616"></a><a name="_Toc7593047"></a><a name="_Toc7593135"></a><a
name="_Toc7837418"></a><a name="_Toc7846489"></a><a name="_Toc7851601"></a><a
name="_Toc7919097"></a><a name="_Toc7919464"></a><a name="_Toc7924653"></a><a
name="_Toc7972139"><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7924653'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919464'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7919097'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7851601'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7846489'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7837418'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593135'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7593047'><span style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7514616'><span
style='mso-bookmark:_Toc7511963'><![if !supportLists]>2.9<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Hard X-ray Telescope (HXT) Detectors</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></h2>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in;mso-list:l2 level1 lfo12'><![if !supportLists]>1.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What are the Level 1 and Level 2 science requirements for the
proposed mission, and how do these motivate the candidate technologies which
will be investigated?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Explain the
connections between the science requirements and the engineering requirements
on those technologies.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The primary science requirements that flow to the HXT
detectors are broad bandpass, energy resolution, and sensitivity, as defined in
section 2.1.6.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>Additional mission requirements that flow to the HXT
detectors include a mass budget.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>2.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What are the significant technological challenges for these
technologies --- i.e., which technical capabilities have not already been
demonstrated?</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='text-indent:0in'>The challenge is to demonstrate
high-quantum efficiency and 5 keV threshold for a 500 micron CdZnTe pixel
detector/low-noise Application-specific Integrated Circuit (ASIC) hybrid.</p>

<p class=bodytextindent style='margin-left:.25in'>To date, CdZnTe pixel sensors
of appropriate dimensions and pixel size have been demonstrated at E&gt;= 10
keV.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>The CdZnTe efficiency
must be measured, and possibly improved upon for energies below 10 keV.<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Low noise ASICs with large numbers of
channels must demonstrate the desired systematic threshold.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>3.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>For each technological challenge, what are the metrics by
which success --- i.e., technical readiness --- is to be measured?</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='text-indent:0in'>Technical readiness will be
measured by making low-energy X-ray scanning measurements of a prototype (at
least 2 cm x 2 cm) detector.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>These
must show the threshold to be below 5 keV, and the QE of the sensor to be above
70%.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>4.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What kinds of demonstrations are required to validate
technical readiness? Will ground testing be sufficient, or are there technical
capabilities which can only be demonstrated in space?</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='text-indent:0in'>Laboratory measurements with
radioactive sources and X-ray generators.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>5.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>What is status of each metric --- i.e., compare the current
capability with the required capability?</p>

<p class=MsoListBullet3 style='text-indent:0in'>Detectors and readouts with
appropriate spatial resolution, energy resolution, and high-energy (E&gt;10
keV) response have been demonstrated.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>The electronic thresholds are at ~8 keV, and low energy QE is unknown.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>6.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Is the required capability a reasonable extension of the
current capability or does it require a significant advancement or new
approach?</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>The critical technologies are reasonable extensions of
existing technologies, as described above.</p>

<p class=MsoListNumber style='text-indent:0in'><![if !supportLists]>7.<span
style='font:7.0pt "Times New Roman"'>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span><![endif]>Is the specific technological challenge being addressed for
other applications?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Identify
technical synergies with other NASA programs if they exist.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>There is significant synergy with a number of balloon
SR&amp;T programs (HEFT, InFocus), with explorer concepts.<span
style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Other missions requiring
high-resolution CdZnTe pixel detectors (e.g., EXIST) are benefitting
substantially from the low-noise readout development, and the high-quality
CdZnTe sensor development.</p>

<p class=MsoBodyText>There is overlap with some balloon programs but none are
driving the requirements in this way..</p>

</div>

EN-US'><br clear=ALL style='page-break-before:always;mso-break-type:section-break'>
